## Domain Knowledge (LLM-generated)
**Domain**: nonlinear oscillations / classical mechanics
**Analysis**: This task models the acceleration of a nonlinear harmonic oscillator, where dv_dt depends on position x (restoring force), velocity v (damping), and possibly time t (driving). Classical nonlinear oscillator equations include Duffing, van der Pol, and parametrically driven systems.

**Common formula structures in this domain**:
- Simple harmonic oscillator: dv_dt = c0 * x (linear restoring force)
- Damped harmonic oscillator: dv_dt = c0 * x + c1 * v (linear restoring + linear damping)
- Duffing oscillator: dv_dt = c0 * x + c1 * x**3 (cubic nonlinear restoring force)
- Damped Duffing oscillator: dv_dt = c0 * x + c1 * x**3 + c2 * v (cubic restoring + damping)
- Van der Pol oscillator: dv_dt = c0 * x + c1 * v + c2 * x**2 * v (amplitude-dependent damping)
- Quintic nonlinearity: dv_dt = c0 * x + c1 * x**3 + c2 * x**5 (higher-order restoring force)
- Driven oscillator: dv_dt = c0 * x + c1 * v + c2 * sin(c3 * t) (periodic external driving)
- Parametric oscillator: dv_dt = c0 * x * cos(c1 * t) (time-modulated stiffness)
- Nonlinear damping: dv_dt = c0 * x + c1 * v * abs(v) (quadratic velocity damping, drag-like)
- Cubic damping + restoring: dv_dt = c0 * x + c1 * x**3 + c2 * v + c3 * v**3 (full cubic nonlinearity)
- Rayleigh oscillator: dv_dt = c0 * x + c1 * v + c2 * v**3 (nonlinear velocity damping)
- Mixed nonlinearity: dv_dt = c0 * x + c1 * x**2 + c2 * x**3 + c3 * v (asymmetric + cubic restoring)
- Driven damped Duffing: dv_dt = c0 * x + c1 * x**3 + c2 * v + c3 * cos(c4 * t) (full Duffing with drive)
- Position-velocity coupling: dv_dt = c0 * x + c1 * x * v + c2 * x**2 * v (generalized nonlinear coupling)

**Formula structure heuristic features**:
- Oscillation damping envelope → Exponential decay envelope f(x)*exp(-c*Abs(x)) for symmetric damped oscillation, Gaussian envelope f(x)*exp(-c*x**2) for localized wave packets
- Saturation/clipping effects → Rational fraction x/(1+x), tanh; for variables with alternating positive/negative in oscillatory systems, selectively apply Abs
- Growth/decay → Exponential growth exp(c*t), Logistic 1/(1+exp(-c*x)), power law x**c
- Threshold/activation behavior → Max(x-c, 0), piecewise functions
- Coupling/cross effects → Product terms between variables x*y, power-law coupling x**c1 * y**c2
- Odd-symmetry restoring forces → polynomial in odd powers of x (c0*x + c1*x**3 + c2*x**5) indicating symmetric potential wells
- Self-sustained oscillations → terms like (c0 + c1*x**2)*v indicating amplitude-dependent damping sign change (van der Pol type)
- Hardening/softening spring → sign of cubic term x**3 relative to linear term x determines whether frequency increases or decreases with amplitude
- Periodic driving forces → sin(c*t) or cos(c*t) terms appearing additively, indicating external energy input
- Parametric excitation → multiplicative coupling between x and trigonometric functions of t, e.g., x*cos(c*t)
- Conservative vs dissipative → absence of v-dependent terms indicates a conservative system derivable from a potential V(x)
- Asymmetric potentials → even powers of x (x**2 terms) in the force indicate broken spatial symmetry
- Limit cycle behavior → competing damping terms with opposite signs at different amplitudes, e.g., c0*v + c1*v**3 with opposite sign coefficients

**GT:** `-0.0589613*v³ - 0.332588*v*(1 - v²) - 0.111444*v*exp(-|x|) + 0.385230*sin(t)`

Let me first expand the GT:
`-0.0589613*v³ - 0.332588*v + 0.332588*v³ - 0.111444*v*exp(-|x|) + 0.385230*sin(t)`

Combining v³ terms: `(0.332588 - 0.058961)*v³ = 0.273627*v³`

So GT = `0.385230*sin(t) + 0.273627*v³ - 0.332588*v - 0.111444*v*exp(-|x|)`

The key terms are:
1. `sin(t)` - sinusoidal in t
2. `v³` - cubic in v
3. `v` - linear in v
4. `v*exp(-|x|)` - v times exponential decay in |x|

The critical challenge is matching `v*exp(-|x|)`. This is an even function of x with exponential decay.

Let me check candidates that have flexible x-dependence multiplied by v:

**Candidates 6, 19-24, 29:** These have terms like `v*(c + x)^c` which could potentially work. If we set `(c7+x)^c8` with appropriate constants... but `exp(-|x|)` is not a power law, and these expressions aren't even functions of x (for non-integer powers). For x > 0, we'd need `(c+x)^p ≈ exp(-x)`, which can't hold for all x.

**Candidates 27-38:** These have `v*x` linear terms, which can't match `v*exp(-|x|)`.

**Candidates with `v/(c+x)²`:** (7-11, 39-43) - These are rational functions of x, not exponential decay. Can't match.

**Candidates with `v*sqrt(x)` and `v*sqrt(c+x)`:** (1, 5, 12-18, 41, 44-47) - These involve square root terms. For x > 0: `c5*v*sqrt(x) + v*sqrt(c6+x)` cannot equal `v*exp(-|x|)` for all x > 0. Square root functions grow, while exp(-|x|) decays.

**Candidate 8:** `c0*sin(c1*t+c2) + c3*v^c4 + c5*v + c6*v³ + c7*v/(c8+x)²`
Setting c3=0 gives `sin + v + v³ + v/(c8+x)²`. The x-dependent term is `v/(c8+x)²` which can't match `v*exp(-|x|)`.

**Candidate 21:** `c0*sin(c1*t+c2) + c3*exp(c4*x) + c5 + c6*v³ + c7*v*(c8+x)^c9`
The `exp(c4*x)` term doesn't multiply v, so it can't produce `v*exp(-|x|)`. The `v*(c8+x)^c9` is a power law, not exponential.

**Candidate 33:** `c0*sin(c1*t+c2) + c3*v^c4 + c5*v + c6 + c7*v³ + c8*x + c9*v*x`
This has `v*x` which is linear in x, can't match exponential decay.

**Candidate 28:** `c0*sin(c1*t+c2) + c3*exp(c4*x) + c5*v + c6 + c7*v³ + c8*x + c9*v*x`
The `exp(c4*x)` doesn't multiply v, and `v*x` is linear. Can't match.

None of the candidates contain a term of the form `v*exp(f(x))` or `v*exp(-|x|)`. The x-dependent terms in the candidates are power laws (`(c+x)^p`), rational functions (`1/(c+x)²`), square roots, linear terms (`v*x`), logarithms, or standalone exponentials not multiplied by v.
